  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5bd56cff-9635-45ba-8e9b-5b025936b4be'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11075288114649385124">„Под игото“ е първият български роман. Подзаглавие - „Из живота на българина в навечерието на Освобождението“.<br/>Написан е от Иван Вазов по време на изгнание в Одеса, пренесен е в България с руската дипломатическа поща. <br/><br/>Композиционно романът се състои от три части и 88 глави, които обхващат подготовката, избухването и потушаването на Априлското въстание. Сюжетното действие за</span>
  <span id="freeText11075288114649385124" style="display:none">„Под игото“ е първият български роман. Подзаглавие - „Из живота на българина в навечерието на Освобождението“.<br />Написан е от Иван Вазов по време на изгнание в Одеса, пренесен е в България с руската дипломатическа поща. <br /><br />Композиционно романът се състои от три части и 88 глави, които обхващат подготовката, избухването и потушаването на Априлското въстание. Сюжетното действие започва с идването на Бойчо Огнянов в Бяла Черква през май 1875 г. и завършва с неговата смърт през май 1876 г. Но фабулата на творбата не се изчерпва с личните драми на героите, нито с действията и противодействията им през тази година, защото не личните, а историческите събития са в основата на сюжетното действие и определят неговия епически характер. Своеобразна кулминация и развръзка на романа са главите "Пиянството на един народ" и "Пробуждане", в които Вазов постига редки за българската литература прозрения по философия на българската история с резките й преходи от опиянение към отрезвяване и страх, от подем към покруса, разочарование и предателство.<br /><br />Романът "Под игото" е първата книга, която носи литературна слава на Вазов и на България. Въпреки някои слабости и противоречия, това е най-мащабната и недостигната още "енциклопедия на българския национален живот".<br /><br />"Под игото" е филмиран през 1953г.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11075288114649385124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_535941874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/535941874" />
    <a title="Scott Cameron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11461824-scott-cameron"><img alt="Scott Cameron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343800762p2/11461824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/535941874?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Cameron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Cameron" href="/user/show/11461824-scott-cameron">Scott Cameron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780543691781" href="/book/show/2445777.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer535941874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253137882035393512">It's not easy to find English translations of Ivan Vazov's writing. Even Under the Yoke, his most famous book, was very difficult to find with this particular translation being over 100 years old. Knowing nothing of the original Bulgarian, it seemed like a fine translation, but it does make a person wonder because it seems to be the only one ever done.<br/><br/>The most interesting part of the book for me is its exploration of what motivates a population to act (or not act). The way that entire villages o</span>
  <span id="freeText8253137882035393512" style="display:none">It's not easy to find English translations of Ivan Vazov's writing. Even Under the Yoke, his most famous book, was very difficult to find with this particular translation being over 100 years old. Knowing nothing of the original Bulgarian, it seemed like a fine translation, but it does make a person wonder because it seems to be the only one ever done.<br /><br />The most interesting part of the book for me is its exploration of what motivates a population to act (or not act). The way that entire villages of people moved in unison with one another, fear spreading like an infection across the group, extinguishing the will to act and turning average people against each other as personal survival becomes the highest goal. The dynamics of how the fizzled rebellion played out struck me as quite true to life, and Vazov's wisdom and insight into human nature shows through. Both heroic and tragic, the book is worth reading even for this perspective alone.<br /><br />Other elements of the story I didn't care for so much. The romantic plot seemed kind of forced and unbelievable, but fortunately wasn't the central theme.<br /><br />Overall, the book is definitely worth checking out if you're interested in the history of Bulgaria. It offers a taste of what life was like in late 19th century Bulgaria under Turkish rule and I quite enjoyed being immersed in it even for a short time. The "Bulgarian spirit" and patriotism comes through forcefully and makes for quite a memorable experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8253137882035393512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1451199934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14600882424463569846">Overall a great book and you can certainly see why this is considered to be THE Bulgarian classic. The story is about a revolt/ revolution. The protagonist (Boicho) saves a fellow Bulgarian father and daughter from certain death at the hands of 2 Turks by killing both of them. He then essentially goes into hiding and throughout the course of his hiding ferments his idea of a revolution. The Bulgarians at that point had been living “under the yolk” of Turkish hegemony and were desperate to free t</span>
  <span id="freeText14600882424463569846" style="display:none">Overall a great book and you can certainly see why this is considered to be THE Bulgarian classic. The story is about a revolt/ revolution. The protagonist (Boicho) saves a fellow Bulgarian father and daughter from certain death at the hands of 2 Turks by killing both of them. He then essentially goes into hiding and throughout the course of his hiding ferments his idea of a revolution. The Bulgarians at that point had been living “under the yolk” of Turkish hegemony and were desperate to free themselves of the oppression which the author describes (but not in that much detail). The story is given a second dimension due to the love story embedded within it between Boicho (aka Ognianoff) and the young Rada who falls in love with him. I wouldn’t want to give too much of the story away but essentially there is a big revolt which Boicho galvanises - the result of which you will have to read yourself. This took me a while to read because the translation was by some dodgy company because ever 10th word was incorrectly typed and also I found it took its time to get going in the middle. There is a lot of action in the start and at the end but it slows right down in the middle. Overall certainly worth a read especially if you are Bulgarian or Turkish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14600882424463569846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2768523901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1085766131128655598">I re-read this book recently in order to see it from the eyes of a young woman as opposed to a teenager. Once again, I was impressed by the fully blooded characters, the realistic description of their motives and feelings. I also loved how the action was well-paced, with plenty of exciting and tensed moments, where favourite characters barely avoided death. The strongest scene was probably the ending, which made me cry as if it was really happening. The only reason I didn’t give the book 5 stars</span>
  <span id="freeText1085766131128655598" style="display:none">I re-read this book recently in order to see it from the eyes of a young woman as opposed to a teenager. Once again, I was impressed by the fully blooded characters, the realistic description of their motives and feelings. I also loved how the action was well-paced, with plenty of exciting and tensed moments, where favourite characters barely avoided death. The strongest scene was probably the ending, which made me cry as if it was really happening. The only reason I didn’t give the book 5 stars is the archaic language which I found difficult to read. <br /><br />I fully recommend to everyone who wants to read this very realistic account of one of the bloodiest periods in Bulgarian history.</span>

<div id="review_2162720402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2162720402?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisajean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisajean" href="/user/show/22100142-lisajean">Lisajean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22100142-lisajean?shelf=russia">russia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22100142-lisajean?shelf=bulgaria">bulgaria</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22100142-lisajean?shelf=1001-book-list">1001-book-list</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2162720402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5257378402933081511"><i>Under the Yoke</i>, the national epic of Bulgaria, was written in 1888 and details the events of the April Uprising against the Turks, which Vazov himself took part in. Although the Uprising failed, it did spark the war that actually won Bulgarian independence. Vazov, himself a heroic figure, was so successful because his work built Bulgarian national consciousness and pride. It helps that there was almost no secular literature in Bulgarian up to that point. However, the book does not stand the test</span>
  <span id="freeText5257378402933081511" style="display:none"><i>Under the Yoke</i>, the national epic of Bulgaria, was written in 1888 and details the events of the April Uprising against the Turks, which Vazov himself took part in. Although the Uprising failed, it did spark the war that actually won Bulgarian independence. Vazov, himself a heroic figure, was so successful because his work built Bulgarian national consciousness and pride. It helps that there was almost no secular literature in Bulgarian up to that point. However, the book does not stand the test of time. There are some nice descriptions of the Balkans and some funny accounts of small town life, but the plot and main characters are too formulaic and overly Romantic. I would recommend this to Bulgarians and people who hate the Turks (same thing?), but not to anyone else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5257378402933081511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1102465431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102465431" />
    <a title="Monty Milne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14797192-monty-milne"><img alt="Monty Milne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363450934p2/14797192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102465431?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monty Milne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monty Milne" href="/user/show/14797192-monty-milne">Monty Milne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784350550" href="/book/show/23242047-under-the-yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102465431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14145682843357085012">What fun to be transported back in time to a Valley of Roses, filled with grotesque bashi-bazouks, "soup" landlords, exotic revolutionaries, scheming monks and remarkably worldly nuns...not to mention a doomed but compelling love story.<br/><br/>Like most Englishmen I sympathise with the Bulgarian revolutionaries but some things struck me which avid Bulgarian nationalists might not like to hear me say...first, the novel makes clear that some Bulgarians were in favour of the Ottoman status quo - a fact whi</span>
  <span id="freeText14145682843357085012" style="display:none">What fun to be transported back in time to a Valley of Roses, filled with grotesque bashi-bazouks, "soup" landlords, exotic revolutionaries, scheming monks and remarkably worldly nuns...not to mention a doomed but compelling love story.<br /><br />Like most Englishmen I sympathise with the Bulgarian revolutionaries but some things struck me which avid Bulgarian nationalists might not like to hear me say...first, the novel makes clear that some Bulgarians were in favour of the Ottoman status quo - a fact which is often airbrushed out of modern Bulgarian history. And second....sorry Mr Vazov, but shooting down a terrified barefoot gypsy and then having your characters make jokes about it makes me feel a bit queasy...<br /><br />You might say the fact that the author describes the "good guys" committing atrocities as well as the "bad guys" is evidence of his honesty and even-handedness - except that I have a sneaking suspicion that he doesn't think the "good guys" have really done anything wrong..<br /><br />Nevertheless this is a brilliant evocation of a fascinating time and place. There are even some passages which made me laugh out loud - for human foibles are universal, and there is no shortage of vivid characters here. <br /><br />My kinsman General Lord Milne was defeated by General Vladimir Vazov - brother of the author - on several occasions in the first world war. After the war, Gen. Vazov was invited to England, and my kinsman complimented him on "waging war in a gentlemanly manner"...I am not sure he would have said the same thing about some of the Bulgarians in this novel....</span>
  <a data-text-id="14145682843357085012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The plot follows the trials and tribulations of an agitator as he struggles to raise the revolution amongst his compatriots. It is fascinating, given that we are living in times where insurrection is organised through social media, to see the sheer time and effort it once required to go from village to village organising meetings and coordinating action through messages and signa</span>
  <span id="freeText8253317833106644903" style="display:none">A stirring tale of insurrection among the towns and villages of Southern Bulgaria against the Turks during the 1870s. The plot follows the trials and tribulations of an agitator as he struggles to raise the revolution amongst his compatriots. It is fascinating, given that we are living in times where insurrection is organised through social media, to see the sheer time and effort it once required to go from village to village organising meetings and coordinating action through messages and signals. There is a it of romance to lighten the story but it mostly gave me an insight into the passion that patriotism gives rise to.</span>

    <a title="StellaDow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44780786-stelladow"><img alt="StellaDow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439049938p2/44780786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer489411339262050945">I found an English translation online at the Internet Archive and managed to start reading it ahead of, and while I was in Bulgaria for the first time. Highly recommended, because it pretty much is the "founding myth" of Bulgaria, gives a good insight into some of the feelings people still have about the Ottoman Empire and also happens to be a fun fast-paced romance. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2389382832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389382832" />
    <a title="Sara &quot;Cristia&quot; H. J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74834802-sara-cristia-h-j"><img alt="Sara &quot;Cristia&quot; H. J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562747664p2/74834802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2389382832?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara &quot;Cristia&quot; H. J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara &quot;Cristia&quot; H. J." href="/user/show/74834802-sara-cristia-h-j">Sara &quot;Cristia&quot; H. J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2389382832&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2389382832" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16761843512754800446">In the tantalizing novel, Under the Yoke, Ivan Vazoff writes about an ill-fated revolution in Bulgaria by the end of the XIX century, when it was under the intolerable Turkish/Ottoman rule.<br/><br/>It tells the story of Boicho Ognianoff, a revolutionist who returned to his country after being imprisoned abroad to join some friends and begin a revolt to free Bulgaria from the Ottoman reign. Under the Yoke describes the idealism of a nation willing to undertake sacrifices for the sake of the whole, but the</span>
  <span id="freeText16761843512754800446" style="display:none">In the tantalizing novel, Under the Yoke, Ivan Vazoff writes about an ill-fated revolution in Bulgaria by the end of the XIX century, when it was under the intolerable Turkish/Ottoman rule.<br /><br />It tells the story of Boicho Ognianoff, a revolutionist who returned to his country after being imprisoned abroad to join some friends and begin a revolt to free Bulgaria from the Ottoman reign. Under the Yoke describes the idealism of a nation willing to undertake sacrifices for the sake of the whole, but the struggle was reckless and without real foundations. It was the shortest fight which costed the lives of many and which served as example for future rebellions.<br /><br />Through his novel, Vazoff hints the misery resulted of such tyranny and the importance of the people's will to assume their duty in defending their nation and reestablish order for a better future. <br /><br />Ognianoff returns to his country with the weak idea, the illusion of revolting villages to seize the enemy out, though his strategy is poor. He manages to gather a big group to prepare for the fight, and he begins a love story with Rada, a simple orphan country girl who works for an imminent governor and who tries to hide Ognianoff in the beginning. But this beautiful love dies very young with the revolution for the many sacrifices Ognianoff and Rada must carry with.<br /><br />Everybody believes that they would be ready to fight when "the national dissatisfaction reaches its utmost limit and the tyranny becomes unbearable."<br />The message is clear: "The more submissive we are, the more they ill-use us." And everybody knows how real that was. So, when times become very difficult, the Resistance stirs up the people to revolt. <br /><br />Everything begins with dissatisfaction. When this happens, gossips and news spread everywhere in form of secret messages through poems, hymns, and stories (among other ways). The calling for revolt is through sabotage and camouflaging to take part of attacks that begin here and there.<br />Then, insurrection becomes the clear result of tyranny.<br /><br />True Patriots will not be defeated by harassment, threats, tortures, etc. But passion is such a weakness when it has no good basis. Vazoff describes the values of a true patriot through his idealistic protagonist by saying: <br />"But so far from his enthusiasm for the ideas for which he had suffered, having been calmed down by exile and suffering, they had made him a still more fervent idealist, bold to madness, frenzied in his love for his country, and chivalrous to the degree of self-sacrifice. Fateful occassions had already shown him to us at work. Aye, he had come to Bulgaria to work for its liberation."<br /><br />Later on, grows a misunderstanding and disagreement between the Patriots. Though they all want to fight the Turkish regime, each group defends different ideas, foolish distinctions. While one group seek liberation from oppression and the freedom of will, Ognianoff and some friends talk about "imposing rules on the nation and annihilate every idea of equality..."<br />To fight a tyranny, the insurrection must focus clearly on a certain object each time and know who the real enemies are. Otherwise, if people cannot depend on their leaders, they'll have to remove them and move on.<br />Rebellions are easier to begin in villages and towns than in cities ... their passion can be easily stirred up, though without strategy and organization, passion is the instrument of suicide.<br /><br />Suddenly, "the idea (of a rebellion) struck its roots everywhere with invincible force, it spreads over...Balkan and valley, over the hut of the poor shepherd and the cell of the monk."<br />"Old and young display equal passion. The peasants left their field unfilled to cast bullets, the citizens neglected their business. Secret posts went day and night between the different committees and the central one..."<br />But for stronger foundations, rebellion should also integrate an intellectual team, and not only force arms, for "thought and soul can only be supplied by the intelligence."<br /><br />However, a lack of planification, organization, and logistic, leads the insurrection towards its destruction. As a result, rebels were gradually losing their courage, because of lack of support from other towns and groups of Resistance, for not having a good communication system among them and a steady plan.<br /><br />"Discouragement and despair gained ground every moment. Discipline was growing weak, complaints, murmurings, regrets, the forerunners of demoralisation replaced enthusiasm of the first days of the revolt."<br />"The revolutionists now resemble an army which has been defeated without a battle...to their moral sufferings were added physical hardship..."<br /><br />It becomes clear that Ognianoff's ideas were based on the illusion of socialism, which led to many disagreements among the compatriots, which faded their courage away. That continued to break down the Resistance essence and comes a point which alludes to criminality (such as that of the Che Guevara) to protecting the revolution. This can be seen when they catch some hostages and kill them. These were Ognianoff's wrong ideas.<br /><br />Revolutionists call to revolt even if it means their ruin. But people wasn't willing to sacrifice their lives for the country, because of fear to death and to protect their families (that's why socialism, as a first and beautiful disguise of communism, can't exist truly in the world. It always ends in mysery). This is when emerges the insurgents' treason and disloyalty, and the regime takes advantages of their weaknesses and bad plans.<br />Traitors emerge, very few brave rebels remain, those who'll become the martyrs.<br /><br />"The revolution ended in capitulation. History furnishes examples of rising as sacred and ill-fated, but none so tragically inglorious ... The April Insurrection was like a still-born child, conceived under the impulse of the most ardent love, and stifled by its mother in horror at its birth ... golden hopes, profound faith, gigantic strength and enthusiasm, the heritage of centuries of suffering, all vanished in a moment. It was a terrible awakening."<br />"Cowardice and treachery are the natural off-spring of an ill-fated revolution."<br /><br />That was why rage and resentment aren't the best means to begin a rebellion. It's not convenient to destroy the enemy by force of arms only. First, rebellion must seek the sympathy of most civilians and of other nations, whereas it means by showing off the suffering, martyrdom, and bloodshed happening inside the country.<br /><br />The end is what impacts the reader as the Resistance don't meet its goal. Instead, the rebellion dies with the murder of Ognianoff, Rada, and many others, while some manage to flee from the country.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16761843512754800446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1610582885342602920">Good book depicting a true historical period when Bulgaria was under the Ottoman yoke (that was honestly the first time I hear this word.. even in Arabic). <br/>I recommend this book as a historical chef-d'oeuvre .. characters are extremely vivid and I like the fact that they evolve and that in general not all "good characters " stay good and vice versa.. <br/>The author was called the father of Bulgarian Literature. He actually is talented in the way he tells a story, keeps you hooked, events are unpredi</span>
  <span id="freeText1610582885342602920" style="display:none">Good book depicting a true historical period when Bulgaria was under the Ottoman yoke (that was honestly the first time I hear this word.. even in Arabic). <br />I recommend this book as a historical chef-d'oeuvre .. characters are extremely vivid and I like the fact that they evolve and that in general not all "good characters " stay good and vice versa.. <br />The author was called the father of Bulgarian Literature. He actually is talented in the way he tells a story, keeps you hooked, events are unpredictable and far from boring, and you could feel his patriotism overflowing his pages. <br />My favorite scene was when Clistoria villagers were fleeing their villlage from the ravaging barbarian Ottomans describing the horrors a human is capable to do caused by survival instinct and fear.. horrible scène. <br />Also.. the realism of the scenario makes you believe that these characters actually existed and the events actually happened..<br /><br />The author has also a real sense of humour and made me feel as if I was actually living with his characters . He also made sure to illustrate Bulgarian traditions, folklore, habits, cities etc..<br /><br />The only reason I rated it 3 stars despite the literary value of the artwork is that I - despite my attachment to the plot- was not really so much attached to the characters and was not moved so much by them. Also ****spoiler please do not read if u have mot read the book***** I expected the end to be more satisfying .. I expected the bad guys to get what they deserve at least hehehe..<br /><br />All in all.. good book worth reading :)</span>

<div id="review_2615565757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2615565757" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38264460-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2615565757?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/38264460-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2615565757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8284055207314223010">Overall, a good story, but an awful edition of it. <br/><br/>The translation I read seems to be one from about a century ago, the first translation of the book into English. In itself, it is a pretty good translation, but differs somewhat from the Bulgarian and Russian versions I appealed to when I wanted clarification. For example, I noticed at some point that a character who had been declared dead at the beginning of part 2 in the English translation was still alive until the 24th chapter of part 2 in t</span>
  <span id="freeText8284055207314223010" style="display:none">Overall, a good story, but an awful edition of it. <br /><br />The translation I read seems to be one from about a century ago, the first translation of the book into English. In itself, it is a pretty good translation, but differs somewhat from the Bulgarian and Russian versions I appealed to when I wanted clarification. For example, I noticed at some point that a character who had been declared dead at the beginning of part 2 in the English translation was still alive until the 24th chapter of part 2 in the Bulgarian/Russian. Apart from that, the translation seems to be abridged and there are numerous chapters that seem to simply not be there—for example, part II chapter 7, which corresponds to part II chapter 16 in the Bulgarian/Russian, jumps immediately to part II chapter 24 of the original; the first two chapters of part II are consolidated into one, smaller chapter. <br /><br />Overall, though, the translation is pretty well written and enjoyable. The real issue I have with the version of the book I read is the excess of typos and mistakes that were present in the Jiahu Books edition, which did not appear in an earlier edition of the same translation that I found on archives.org. The Jiahu edition was simply riddled with errors, as though they had scanned a physical copy and used some software to digitize it without proofing at all. The most common mistake was with quotation marks, which almost never were properly placed; the most distracting mistake was when words were rendered as other words that look kind of similar (e.g. torn might appear as tom). At one point in part II a sentence abruptly cuts off and the following sentence begins halfway through. <br /><br />In short, while Under the Yoke is a good book that I would absolutely recommend, I would strenuously urge anyone to not buy the Jiahu Books copy of it, and I will personally be hesitant to buy any of their books again. (As I mentioned, there is a version you can access for free on archive.org, which is not riddled with errors.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8284055207314223010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2669642386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669642386" />
    <a title="Richard Thompson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11657479-richard-thompson"><img alt="Richard Thompson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530711053p2/11657479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669642386?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Thompson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Thompson" href="/user/show/11657479-richard-thompson">Richard Thompson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11657479-richard-thompson?shelf=eastern-european-literature">eastern-european-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669642386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5449020346354137802">This is the great national novel of Bulgaria. I have already read and enjoyed the great national novel of Azerbaijan (Ali and Nino), the great national epic poem of Poland (Pan Tadeusz), the great national novel of Armenia (Forty Days of Musa Dagh), and the great national novel of the Don Cossacks (Quiet Flows the Don), so I was hoping for another fine story of downtrodden people of Eastern Europe in rebellion against oppression. In this regard it did not disappoint. There is heroic scheming and</span>
  <span id="freeText5449020346354137802" style="display:none">This is the great national novel of Bulgaria. I have already read and enjoyed the great national novel of Azerbaijan (Ali and Nino), the great national epic poem of Poland (Pan Tadeusz), the great national novel of Armenia (Forty Days of Musa Dagh), and the great national novel of the Don Cossacks (Quiet Flows the Don), so I was hoping for another fine story of downtrodden people of Eastern Europe in rebellion against oppression. In this regard it did not disappoint. There is heroic scheming and fighting, love, sacrifice and tragic death -- everything that the doctor ordered. The beautiful bucolic setting is nicely described. The characters are nicely drawn though a little stock in their portrayals. And Vazov deserves great credit for creating the literary language of Bulgarian, which basically didn't exist before him. In this sense he is the Chaucer/Shakespeare of Bulgaria. It is not an easy thing to do to create a literary form out a folk vernacular, but the expressiveness of Vazov's language comes out even in translation. <br /><br />Still there are things to not like so much here. The plot is a bit by the numbers. The Turks are comic book villians -- evil and stupid beyond belief so that it is hard to see them as real people. The book would have been much better if the enemy had been more human and worthy. And when the Bulgarians are briefly in charge, they brutally murder one of their prisoners without the slightest blink of an eye as to the morality of the killing. It makes it harder to be fully on the side of the Bulgarians.<br /><br />I'm not going to go learn Bulgarian so that I can read the rest of Vazov's work, but still overall this was pretty good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5449020346354137802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3072331641155906184" style="display:none">Under the Yoke (Под игото) is a classic of the times. What makes this book amazing is the writing by Vazov, is poetic, its energetic,the descriptions are so vivid and flow like wind in the sky. If you speak Bulgarian its truly something that you will experience. I personality have not read the English as im trying to dive into the meaning of the book in its originality (in Bulgarian, but I'm glad there is still a version for non-Bulgarians that can be enjoyed. To my fellow Bulgarians, read the original not the new Bulgarian translation as it undervalues the beauty of the book and in my opinion hurt Vazov's poetic writing.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2732078008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732078008" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10403404-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340370885p2/10403404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732078008?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/10403404-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789549403015" href="/book/show/897120.Under_the_Yoke">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10403404-matt?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10403404-matt?shelf=war-fiction">war-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10403404-matt?shelf=realist-fiction">realist-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732078008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1061160184534430578"><i>Full review can be read here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.com/2019/10/vazovs-under-yoke.html'>https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.c...</a></i><br/><br/><i>Under the Yoke</i> was actually published in Britain before it reached native audiences in Bulgaria, and it had an undeniable impact. The sympathy and the pity that was roused in Morris’s noble breast for the Bulgarians can be felt in Ivan Vazov’s prose in every page, nearly every sentence. In terms of its sheer literary quality, it’s masterful, and suffers only from a few traces of turgidity. It deftly combines elements of satiri</span>
  <span id="freeText1061160184534430578" style="display:none"><i>Full review can be read here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.com/2019/10/vazovs-under-yoke.html">https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.c...</a></i><br /><br /><i>Under the Yoke</i> was actually published in Britain before it reached native audiences in Bulgaria, and it had an undeniable impact. The sympathy and the pity that was roused in Morris’s noble breast for the Bulgarians can be felt in Ivan Vazov’s prose in every page, nearly every sentence. In terms of its sheer literary quality, it’s masterful, and suffers only from a few traces of turgidity. It deftly combines elements of satirical comedy with its overall tragœdian outlook. It explores the natures of heroism and cowardice – both moral and physical. It draws somewhat caricatured, yet vivid and poignant, images of the political trends in Vazov’s Bulgaria, in ways that remind one strongly of the writing of Nikolai Gogol – <a href="https://www.gutenberg.org/files/1197/1197-h/1197-h.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Taras Bulba</i>
</a> in particular. It spends time to portray the inward lives and commitments of its protagonists – particularly Boicho Ognyanov and Doctor Sokolov, the two primary revolutionaries – in ways that show Vazov to have been a pupil also of Dostoevsky. <br /><br />Yes – Vazov was incontrovertibly a literary Russophile. He himself is not coy about showing it, with Dostoevsky’s name being mentioned at several places in the text. But his work is quite original in that it explores the peculiarities of the Bulgarian situation in lights that can be unflattering. He muses deeply on what might have caused the rebellion to succeed or fail, what caused one village to take up arms against the Turks and another to surrender. He depicts the soaring hopes of the Bulgarian revolutionaries and the ordinary people that followed them. He also does not shy away from the grisly realities of defeat, meaning not only genocide and (not uncommonly) rape as weapons of war, but also the more pathetic realities of informing, favour-currying and backstabbing that were the means of self-preservation among a populace that had much to fear from Turkish repression.<br /><br />But what struck me the most strongly about the text was Vazov’s tacit understanding of the folk-poetics of the desperate. Here he does not come off as necessarily a literary Russophile, but he does observe the folk tradition with the appreciative eye of one of his British near-contemporaries like <a href="https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.com/2010/12/reflection-on-nation-part-2.html" rel="nofollow noopener">GK Chesterton</a> or <a href="https://heavyangloorthodox.blogspot.com/2019/01/happy-birthday-to-tollers-happy-landing.html" rel="nofollow noopener">JRR Tolkien</a>...<br /><br />I still feel as though I have not done a very great service to <i>Under the Yoke</i>. I have dwelt here mainly on the conscious similarities Vazov’s writing has to a most <i>un-</i>revolutionary author in another country. And yet it is a martial epic tragœdy – a revolutionary epic tragœdy. It dwells profoundly on the paired themes of revenge and forgiveness, honour and degradation, in such a way that even someone who is not particularly inclined to nationalism must be stirred, if he has a heart at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1061160184534430578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MviMEn0GPDpYWCyblUnu4qrdC1Uk1V15LW3oCdHj+J/2sQCg3hotZFq9HkqToGBPbMx96UtuohQWxP5SbJaaKQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/FiRUUXdDxLoGwrfMrIc3oBsbY7ah+P6AXRIeJbTAVk4ER3j5sEeTOr+OA40W5JzRn0bMrU8HJc63V4jK6Zj7w==')})
  }

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2124105._"><img alt="Тютюн" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1366473906l/2124105._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_2124105'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2124105._?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Тютюн<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7021962._?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Димитър Димов<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.40 avg rating &mdash; 5,909 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1951\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11062249416887235185\">Първо издание на оригинала.\n\nПрез 1946 г. е отпечатан първият откъс от романа „Тютюн“ („Литературен фронт“, № 2, 28.09.1946), озаглавен „Тютюнев склад“. 2 години по-късно излиза нов откъс — „Двубой“ („Литературен фронт“, №20, 31.01.1948), след още 1 <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11062249416887235185\" style=\"display:none\">Първо издание на оригинала.\n\nПрез 1946 г. е отпечатан първият откъс от романа „Тютюн“ („Литературен фронт“, № 2, 28.09.1946), озаглавен „Тютюнев склад“. 2 години по-късно излиза нов откъс — „Двубой“ („Литературен фронт“, №20, 31.01.1948), след още 1 г. — „Тютюн“ (глава от роман) в сп. „Септември“ (1949, № 7). През 1951 романът е завършен окончателно, предаден в издателство „Народна култура“ и в края на 1951 стига до читателите и до своите „злополучни критици“.\n„Тютюн“ се оказва не само един от най-четените романи в българската литература, но и спъни-камъкът на българската марксическа критика. Популярността му напуска романовото пространство и обсебва всичко за и около творбата. Започнал с тридневното „обсъждане“ на „Тютюн“ (8, 11 и 13.02.1952) в СБП, спорът се пренася в периодичния печат („Лит. фронт“, № 10. б.03.1952, и № 11, 13.03.1952) и кулминира в редакционната статия на в. „Работническо дело“ — „За романа \`Тютюн\` и неговите злополучни критици“ (16.03.1952) — спор не толкова за достойнствата на романа, колкото за границите и възможностите на догматичното литературоведско мислене.\nЕдинодушно изказаното мнение, че „Тютюн“ се нуждае от „преработване“, настойчивите подканвания, дългите обсъждания и оказаният натиск карат Димитър Димов, макар и с неохота, да се съгласи да промени романа си, като разшири описанието на работническия свят и въведе нови герои; това увеличава обема на книгата с нови 250 страници. Работата по II редакция протича съвместно с ангажирания от изд. „Народна култура“ литературен критик Яко Молхов — редактор и помощник на Димов през 1953 г., а през 1954 г. „Тютюн“ се появява в новия си вид. През 1955 излиза III издание на романа, в което Д. Димов извършва допълнигелни поправки върху текста, но и в двата случая литературната критика предпочита да се дистанцира от категорични преценки. В крайна сметка „Тютюн“ заживява в новия си вариант и едва през 1992 се появява отново в първоначалния си образ.\nВ различните си редакции „Тютюн“ е роман и за ужасната самотност на личността в капиталистическото общество, за огромния натиск на живота върху нравствените принципи в света на капитала, и за историческата обреченост на олигархиите в България, за социалнопсихологическите причини за тяхната гибел; роман и за потиснатите от монопола на тези олигархии, за техните икономически и политически борби, и за сложния психологичен лабиринт на човешките взаимоотношения както в зловещия свят на „Никотиана“\`, така и извън него. Романът е екранизиран през 1961 (режисьор Н. Корабов). До 1962 година целият роман е преведен на 10 езика (китайски, латвийски, немски, полски, румънски, руски, словашки, украински, унгарски и чешки), а части от него са преведени на английски, арабски, есперанто, испански, италиански и френски.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11062249416887235185\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16877882.Ivan_Vazov"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1522098969p3/16877882.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6959682935544208197">Ivan Minchov Vazov was a Bulgarian poet, novelist and playwright, often referred to as "the Patriarch of Bulgarian literature". He was born in Sopot, a town in the Rose Valley of Bulgaria (then part of the Ottoman Empire). The works of Ivan Vazov reveal two historical epochs - the Bulgarian Renaissance and the Post-Liberation (from Ottoman Empire rule) epoch. Ivan Vazov holds the highest honorary </span>
  <span id="freeText6959682935544208197" style="display:none">Ivan Minchov Vazov was a Bulgarian poet, novelist and playwright, often referred to as "the Patriarch of Bulgarian literature". He was born in Sopot, a town in the Rose Valley of Bulgaria (then part of the Ottoman Empire). The works of Ivan Vazov reveal two historical epochs - the Bulgarian Renaissance and the Post-Liberation (from Ottoman Empire rule) epoch. Ivan Vazov holds the highest honorary title of the Bulgarian Academy of Sciences - Academician. He acted as Education and People Enlightenment Minister from September 7, 1897 until January 30th, 1899, representing the People's Party.<br /><br />Vazov was probably heavily influenced by Botev, who was the ideological leader of the Bulgarian revolutionary movement. He started writing his famous poems with Botev and some other Bulgarian emigrants in Romania. In 1876 he published his first work, Priaporetz and Gusla, followed by "Bulgaria's Sorrows" in 1877.<br /><br />Bulgaria regained its independence in 1878 as a result of the Russo-Turkish War and Vazov wrote the famous Epic of the Forgotten. He became the editor of the political reviews Science and Dawn. He was, however, forced into exile once again, this time to Odessa, because of the persecution of the russophile political faction. Returning to Bulgaria with the help of his mother Suba Vazova, he started teaching. Vazov's next stay was in Svishtov, where he became a civil servant.<br /><br />n 1917 he was nominated for the Nobel Prize in literature</span>
  <a data-text-id="6959682935544208197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
